## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-19 18:44:36]*

<details>
<summary>🔧 Tool: Read -- `document-registry.ts`</summary>

**Input:**

```json
{
  "file_path": "/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/lib/document-registry.ts",
  "limit": 80,
  "offset": 1
}
```

**Result:**

     1→/**  
     2→ * Document Registry - File-based CRUD for team document persistence  
     3→ *  
     4→ * Storage: ~/.aimaestro/teams/docs-{teamId}.json (one per team)  
     5→ * Mirrors the pattern from lib/task-registry.ts  
     6→ */  
     7→  
     8→import fs from 'fs'  
     9→import path from 'path'  
    10→import os from 'os'  
    11→import { v4 as uuidv4 } from 'uuid'  
    12→import { withLock } from '@/lib/file-lock'  
    13→import type { TeamDocument, TeamDocumentsFile } from '@/types/document'  
    14→  
    15→const TEAMS_DIR = path.join(os.homedir(), '.aimaestro', 'teams')  
    16→  
    17→function ensureTeamsDir() {  
    18→  if (!fs.existsSync(TEAMS_DIR)) {  
    19→    fs.mkdirSync(TEAMS_DIR, { recursive: true })  
    20→  }  
    21→}  
    22→  
    23→function docsFilePath(teamId: string): string {  
    24→  // Validate teamId is a strict UUID to prevent path traversal (CC-001)  
    25→  if (!/^[0-9a-f]{8}-[0-9a-f]{4}-[0-9a-f]{4}-[0-9a-f]{4}-[0-9a-f]{12}$/i.test(teamId))  
    26→    throw new Error('Invalid team ID')  
    27→  // path.basename() as defense-in-depth against directory traversal  
    28→  return path.join(TEAMS_DIR, path.basename(`docs-${teamId}.json`))  
    29→}  
    30→  
    31→export function loadDocuments(teamId: string): TeamDocument[] {  
    32→  try {  
    33→    ensureTeamsDir()  
    34→    const filePath = docsFilePath(teamId)  
    35→    if (!fs.existsSync(filePath)) {  
    36→      return []  
    37→    }  
    38→    const data = fs.readFileSync(filePath, 'utf-8')  
    39→    const parsed: TeamDocumentsFile = JSON.parse(data)  
    40→    return Array.isArray(parsed.documents) ? parsed.documents : []  
    41→  } catch (error) {

   116→    const filtered = documents.filter(d => d.id !== docId)  
   117→    if (filtered.length === documents.length) return false  
   118→    saveDocuments(teamId, filtered)  
   119→    return true  
   120→  })

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-19 18:44:45]*

<details>
<summary>🔧 Tool: Read -- `file-lock.ts`</summary>

**Input:**

```json
{
  "file_path": "/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/lib/file-lock.ts",
  "offset": 1,
  "limit": 50
}
```

**Result:**

     1→/**  
     2→ * File Lock — in-process mutex for serializing load→modify→save operations  
     3→ *  
     4→ * Prevents concurrent read-modify-write races within a single Node.js process.  
     5→ * Each registry file gets its own named lock. When one API request is mid-write,  
     6→ * other requests for the same file queue up and run sequentially.  
     7→ *  
     8→ * This is sufficient for Phase 1 (single Next.js process, localhost).  
     9→ * For multi-process deployments, replace with advisory file locks (e.g., proper-lockfile).  
    10→ */  
    11→  
    12→/**  
    13→ * LOCK ORDERING INVARIANT:  
    14→ * When acquiring multiple locks, always acquire in this order:  
    15→ *   1. 'teams'  
    16→ *   2. 'transfers'  
    17→ *   3. 'governance'  
    18→ * Violating this order will cause deadlock.  
    19→ *  
    20→ * Current nested lock usage:  
    21→ * - transfers/[id]/resolve/route.ts: acquires 'teams' then 'transfers' (via resolveTransferRequest)  
    22→ */  
    23→  
    24→// Map of lock name -> queue of pending resolve callbacks  
    25→const locks = new Map<string, Array<() => void>>()  
    26→// Set of currently held lock names  
    27→const held = new Set<string>()  
    28→  
    29→/**  
    30→ * Acquire a named lock. Returns a release function.  
    31→ * If the lock is already held, the caller awaits until it is released.  
    32→ */  
    33→export function acquireLock(name: string): Promise<() => void> {  
    34→  if (!held.has(name)) {  
    35→    // Lock is free — acquire immediately  
    36→    held.add(name)  
    37→    return Promise.resolve(() => releaseLock(name))  
    38→  }  
    39→  
    40→  // Lock is held — enqueue and wait  
    41→  return new Promise<() => void>((resolve) => {  
    42→    if (!locks.has(name)) {  
    43→      locks.set(name, [])  
    44→    }  
    45→    locks.get(name)!.push(() => {  
    46→      resolve(() => releaseLock(name))  
    47→    })  
    48→  })  
    49→}  
    50→  

</details>


## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-19 18:44:48]*

<details>
<summary>🔧 Tool: Read -- `file-lock.ts`</summary>

**Input:**

```json
{
  "file_path": "/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/lib/file-lock.ts",
  "offset": 50,
  "limit": 40
}
```

**Result:**

    50→  
    51→/**  
    52→ * Release a named lock and wake the next waiter if any.  
    53→ */  
    54→function releaseLock(name: string): void {  
    55→  const queue = locks.get(name)  
    56→  if (queue && queue.length > 0) {  
    57→    // Hand lock to next waiter (don't remove from held set)  
    58→    const next = queue.shift()!  
    59→    if (queue.length === 0) {  
    60→      locks.delete(name)  
    61→    }  
    62→    next()  
    63→  } else {  
    64→    // No waiters — release the lock  
    65→    held.delete(name)  
    66→    locks.delete(name)  
    67→  }  
    68→}  
    69→  
    70→/**  
    71→ * Run a function under a named lock.  
    72→ * Convenience wrapper: acquires, runs fn, releases (even on error).  
    73→ *  
    74→ * Note: No deadlock detection or lock timeout.  
    75→ * Lock ordering convention: 'teams' before 'transfers' before 'governance'  
    76→ */  
    77→export async function withLock<T>(name: string, fn: () => T | Promise<T>): Promise<T> {  
    78→  const release = await acquireLock(name)  
    79→  try {  
    80→    return await fn()  
    81→  } finally {  
    82→    release()  
    83→  }  
    84→}  
    85→  

</details>

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-19 18:45:51]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

All 27 tests pass. The two root causes were:  

1. **Missing `@/lib/file-lock` mock**: `createDocument`, `updateDocument`, and `deleteDocument` all use `withLock()` which wasn't mocked, so those functions failed silently or behaved unexpectedly.  

2. **Non-UUID team IDs**: The `docsFilePath()` function now requires strict UUID format (`/^[0-9a-f]{8}-...-[0-9a-f]{12}$/i`), but the tests used `team-1`, `team-a`, etc. which threw `Error('Invalid team ID')` and got caught by the error handlers, returning empty arrays/false/null.  

[DONE] fix-document-registry-tests - Fixed 14 failing tests: added `@/lib/file-lock` mock for `withLock`, replaced all non-UUID team IDs (`team-1`, `team-a`, etc.) with valid UUID constants. All 27 tests now pass.
